Spring and Autumn

Little West Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Becoming a Merchant Entering the Folk Road Returning to Yongshou Leaving Home The Heavenly Person Arriving in Chang'an

What is called a bus station, you may find it funny, is actually widening the shop door a bit so that buses can drive in when they are free. In the courtyard, several earthen houses are connected, and the outer walls allow cars to drive into the houses. Since the houses are gone, behind the courtyard is an upright earthen slope with several semi-oval caves dug into it. These caves are kiln caves. Needless to say, going inside to rest, even standing outside, the dark depths emit an unpleasant smell. But if you don't go in, there is no other place to rest your feet. There's no choice but to harden your heart and carry your luggage inside. Fortunately, I brought a folding camp bed to set up on the earthen pit and sleep. At least I'm not touching the dirt on all sides. When it comes to eating, another problem arises. In the Qianzhou area, pork and eggs can always be bought. But here, neither is available. Fortunately, the shop still has twenty or so black flour buns left that they can sell to me. I said it doesn't matter if there are no vegetables, just buy some white sugar to dip the black buns in and eat. I discussed this with the shopkeeper, and he laughed, saying that if I wanted to eat white sugar, I would have to run back twenty miles to the military supervisor town to buy it. I thought, how could a proper county town not have white sugar? I suspected that the shopkeeper was lying. The next day, I got up early and went into the city to take a look. Who knew that these dozen or so households outside the city were the essence of the entire county. Inside the city was a main road between two earthen hills. The city wall, with pieces missing, circled half of the earthen hilltop, even smaller than the large village I saw in Henan. Climbing up the earthen hill and looking at the entire city, there were wheat fields planted high and low on the hillside. To the north, there were two households: an elementary school and the company headquarters of the city garrison. To the south, there were two households: a deserted old county government office and a city god temple. Besides these, there were only a few kiln caves used as official residences. According to my subsequent investigation, the entire city, including the yin-yang government, consisted of eight households in total. (28)

Schoolbag

— Hua Ling

We Chinese are, after all, a land of literature, so even the (schoolbag) alone has various different styles, as well as a history of change and evolution.

I haven't heard or seen what schoolbags looked like during the Tang, Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties, so I wouldn't dare make wild guesses. But it is said that during the Daoguang, Xianfeng, Tongzhi, and Guangxu periods, our great-grandfathers and grandfathers used only a square of blue cloth, about four square feet in size, and a blue cloth strap.

This kind of schoolbag has now disappeared. I'm afraid it can't even be found in the ancient relics museum. When we went to school, blue cloth schoolbags were no longer used. The books were wrapped in rice-colored feather yarn and clipped under the arm with a hairpin or button. It was very fashionable. This was the schoolbag of the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic of China.

After the revolution, schoolbags also underwent a revolution, abandoning the parcel style and adopting leather schoolbag straps. The narrow leather strap held the books tightly, and anyone could clearly see what books were inside. So everyone loved to carry a few Western-style books to show an indescribable glory.

Leather schoolbag straps were most suitable for university students, so elementary school students used a schoolbag like a postman's mailbag, partly for convenience and partly to hide what books were inside.

Leather schoolbag straps became outdated, and small suitcases took their place. Students of all levels switched to small suitcases, especially girls, because they could hide plenty of cosmetics inside.

But modern university students all use briefcases as schoolbags.

Tidbits

— (Jian Fen)

(Studying) is like eating an olive; the initial taste is bitter, but what follows the bitterness is an indescribable sweetness.

When working, one often feels that one's knowledge is insufficient for application; however, when (studying), one often feels that (studying) is a tedious task.

Shaoxing Women's Filial Hair Bun

— Shijiu

Upon arriving in Shaoxing, the first thing that strikes one is the manure tanks in front of every household and the remnants of the feudal era, such as plaques with inscriptions like "(Residence of a) Grandee" and "Brothers Achieving Degrees Together." Secondly, one should note the women's hair buns worn for mourning.

Shaoxing women rarely cut their hair. Behind their heads, they all retain a round hair bun. This refers to women who are not in mourning. If they are in mourning, they tightly wrap the hair bun with white string, neatly and methodically. There is nothing strange about this kind of white bun; it can be seen in Hangzhou and other places as well. What is striking is that the Shaoxing women's mourning buns also have a semi-circular frame tied on top, towering shakily above their heads. Viewed from behind, the entire white bun looks like a small gong; the semi-circular frame looks like a rope threaded through the gong, with a hand holding it in the air.

I don't know what the use of this semi-circular frame on the white bun is. If it is for aesthetic reasons, it doesn't seem to be so. According to my thinking, this is probably still a remnant of when women were taken as spoils of war. In the past, women have always been regarded by men as the same as livestock, and could be plundered at will. Of course, it would not work to pull them along by their hands and feet; therefore, one could only drag them by their hair. Later, the men became clever and felt that dragging the hair was also not a good idea, so they tied the women's hair into a round knot. In this way, whether lifting or dragging, it seemed much more convenient. This is the same as when we buy a chicken or duck, and holding its wings is tiring, it is better to tie its legs with a straw rope, tie a round knot at one end, and then hang it upside down in the hand. Over time, women also forgot that the round knot on their hair bun was for men to plunder, so they combed it especially neatly, like the mourning buns seen in Shaoxing today.

The above is my speculation, I don't know if it is correct. If it is correct, then women are truly pitiful. As for women who are not in mourning, the reason why they do not add a semi-circular frame to their buns is probably a mark of "(property being) owned."

The Student Trilogy - Part Three (University Era)

Reflections on Japanese and Manchurian Enterprises (Part 2)

— Tianxu Wosheng

Without food and clothing, one will freeze and starve to death, but if there is a source of food and clothing, and life continues, then descendants will inherit the industry, which means that life can continue endlessly. Airplanes and bombs can kill people and destroy objects, but they cannot exterminate our race or destroy our life force, so what is there to fear? If the human heart does not die, then there is no place where one cannot live. Nothing is more sorrowful than the death of the heart, and people today are only seeking life in a dead end, and are ignorant of the way to seek life, abandoning the fundamental for the superficial, which is truly a terminal illness. In the "Tidbits" of the "Spring and Autumn" column, someone said that propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame are certainly miraculous remedies for saving the world, but unfortunately there is a prescription but no medicine. They do not know that medicines are originally abundant in the universe, waiting for people to use them, just like the five grains and six domestic animals, although they are born from nature, they also need to be raised by people. Instead of seeking this, they must be like Emperor Qin seeking immortality overseas. Even if they can achieve abstinence and become immortal, after their corpse decomposes, the soul does not die, and the immortal still wants to descend to earth, which is nothing more than a repeated cycle. Therefore, the reversal of extremes is an inevitable principle. Propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame have reached the extreme of being completely eliminated in recent years, so it is only natural that they will be reborn like yin at the summer solstice and yang at the winter solstice. If we use medicinal prescriptions as a comparison, then there is no difference between Chinese and Western medical principles, but there are many who know that it is so but do not know why. The Japanese managing the Northeast is precisely using our country's prescriptions, utilizing the medicinal materials in our mountains and underground, to save their country from poverty and disease, while we must seek overseas immortal prescriptions, looking for medicines that we do not have, and instead use the medicines we have to provide for others' giving and taking. I truly cannot understand this after a hundred thoughts, so I write this chaotic note prompted by a few lines of report, to offer it for the "Spring and Autumn" brush to abridge, and also to leave it for my wandering life.

Little Knowledge

How to Remove Stains from Clothes

— Qingzhuang

If you carelessly get stains on your clothes, you must feel very upset. Now I will tell you a convenient way to remove these stains.

If the stains have been there for too long, then it will be difficult to completely remove them; you can only make them faint enough to deceive people's eyes. Therefore, to remove stains, it is best to do it as soon as possible, otherwise it may be difficult.

There are only two ways to remove stains: mechanical and chemical; in chemical methods, they can be divided into dry methods and wet methods. The volatile chemicals used in the dry method should preferably not interfere with the fiber and dyed colors.

Now I will write down the types of stains and the methods of removal below: 丨丨

Oil Stains: Oil and grease stains are often mechanically attached. These stains can be removed with red oil and soap solution or Benzene.

Wax Resin: After drying, gradually remove most of it with a small knife, then apply Benzene, wait for a while, and rub vigorously. If it still cannot be removed, then mix magnesium oxide and Benzene into a circular object, apply it to the stain, and brush it off after it is dry. Then the stain can be completely removed, and it will not interfere with the color.

Rust Stains: In summer, white summer clothes often have small yellow spots, which ordinary people mistakenly believe to be fly droppings. If they are faint marks, they can be washed off with a concentrated solution of acetic acid and oxalic acid. If they are deep and dark marks, then first apply tin powder to the stain, and then treat it with acetic acid and oxalic acid using the same method as above; if it still cannot be removed, then first moisten the stain with warm water, then apply a mixture of citric acid and tartaric acid, and then wash it off with water; however, the above three methods cannot be applied to colored clothes. If colored clothes have rust stains, then you can mix soap water and glycerin and apply it to the stained area, leave it for two to three hours, and most of it can be removed. It will be clean after washing.

Ink Stains: Ink stains other than black can be removed by washing with soap, but this method cannot be applied to colored objects. For ink stains on colored objects, use alcohol and an equal amount of iodine water and apply it with a pen, 丨丨 need to apply it several times 丨丨 can mostly eliminate it. If it is white cotton fabric, then after using the above method, bleach it with bleaching powder. If it is silk or wool fabric, then wash it with a mixture of iodine water and soap solution, or add zinc powder to acidic sodium sulfite solution and shake it, then moisten the stained area with this solution, and it can be removed after slight heating.

Black Ink Stains: After washing with soap solution, treat it with the iron rust stain treatment method, and the marks can be removed, because black ink contains iron.

Mold Stains: After drying, brush it clean with a brush, and then wash it with a thin solution of iodine water, and most of it can be removed, but if the discoloration is caused by mold spots, then the marks are simply impossible to completely eliminate.

Sweat Stains: If it hasn't been too long, then it can be removed by washing with water, otherwise, wash it with iodine water.

Fruit Juice Stains: Wash with a mixed solution of borax water and iodine water. If it cannot be removed, then use the bleaching method.

Wine and Sugar Stains: If it hasn't been too long, use water first, otherwise, treat it with the fruit juice stain removal method. If too much time has passed, it cannot be removed.

Tobacco Tar Stains: Remove with wax gourd juice and winter melon juice.

Blood Stains: Moisten the stain with milk and then absorb it with blotting paper.

Ink Stains: Apply a thick glue solution to the stained area, scrape it off carefully with a small knife after it is dry, or wash it with a small amount of salt water, then rub it with rice grains, and finally wash it with water. This method has the best results, but it often damages the fabric.

Record of Fragrant Clouds

— Originally by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

This is certainly very disappointing! In fact, these kinds of formalities are very ordinary for the Empress Dowager, part of her daily life. There's not a day without them, and they practically surround the Empress Dowager everywhere, not letting her have a moment of peace. However, the situation is somewhat different. In the past, the many rituals performed in the palace all day and night, although said to be because the Empress Dowager herself was unwilling to relax too much, were always very solemn in form. But in any case, everyone could not permanently maintain the tense and active spirit of this overly skilled performance. This time, during the welcoming ceremony held at Tianjin Station, everyone felt a relatively excited mood, like people feeling every time they encounter some festive day. What was especially different was that almost everyone had some of the joy of travel, revealed in their expressions.

Although the Empress Dowager was now also sitting upright in her small court on the train, her line of sight was no longer concentrated on the many jade and antique trinkets held by the small wooden shelves on the car wall; she was just watching that lucky little dog and those two newly arrived parrots without blinking. Her intention seemed to be to know what special actions the dog would do when it saw the parrots, and the parrots would do when they saw the dog. Even I was full of hope that these two kinds of animals, now that they had been placed together, would inevitably have new incidents occurring in this small court. Who knew that the reality was exactly the opposite of the ideal; the dog had no interest in the parrots at all, as if it had not seen them. This has already proven that although the dog has a somewhat more peculiar appearance, its intelligence is still no different from that of ordinary dogs, 丨丨 perhaps even more stupid. I really don't understand why the Empress Dowager alone likes it? (138)

Detailed Record of Tung Wah's Victory over Zhenhuan in the Sensational Football Match in Peiping

Three to One, Zhenhuan Recaptured a Goal at the End

(Peiping Special Dispatch) Shanghai's Tung Wah Football Team clashed with Zhenhuan Football Team for the first time in Peiping today (27th). The battle began at 4:30 PM at the Fire Brigade football field. It was indeed a fierce battle. More than 5,000 Peiping citizens who admired their names went to watch. The Fire Brigade field was so crowded that the entrance was impenetrable, and the scene of bustling traffic was unprecedented. Tickets were priced at sixty cents and thirty cents respectively, which was not cheap, but the number of tickets sold that day was no less than 4,000. The four sides of the field were surrounded by railings, and the stands on the south side were densely packed with heads. Those who arrived late had no place to stand. Just after 4 o'clock, the players from both sides successively came onto the field. After briefly testing their footwork, the game began. Wang Zhensheng was the referee. He raised his arm high, and with a "嘎" sound, the silver whistle blew long. The athletes on both sides each secured their positions, and in an instant, the personnel and horses arrived together, and the killing intent lurked. The original formations of both sides were as follows:

Tung Wah Team

Lu Zhongen, Li Ning, Guan Xun'an, Chen Hongguang, Feng Yunyou, Zhao Aisheng (Down), Feng Nianhan (Up)

Wan Xianghua, Li Yiju, Dai Linjing, Chen Jiaqiu, Fu Zhibin

Zhenhuan Team

Wang Yumin, Jin Adu, Chuan Xinqiu, Xu Feimin (Down), Lin Songfa (Up), An Yuansheng, Li Fenglou

Wu Guicheng, Yan Chengkuan, Lian Xuanxun, Wang Jingxi, Zhang Zhizhen (Up), Tang Guoliang (Down)

Tung Wah attacked from the east, and Zhenhuan attacked from the west. Cao Qiuting, on the right wing of Tung Wah, was injured in the leg during a match in Shanghai and has not yet recovered, so he did not play and was replaced by Fu Zhibin, which reduced his strength a lot. Zhenhuan's lineup had no major changes. Opening the lineup, several melee battles were indistinguishable. However, Zhenhuan took the offensive, approaching the enemy's position twice, but unfortunately did not hit. Tung Wah's team was indeed veterans. They were unwilling to work hard unless they encountered a strong enemy. Zhenhuan boldly invaded, and that's when they perked up. The vanguard tightened the reins, and the center forward responded on the road. With one burst of energy, they rushed forward. Feng Yunyou advanced in the middle, and Dai Linjing and Li Yichen assisted from the left and right.

Experiencing two dangerous situations, Zhenhuan also changed its approach, calling back the three armies and intensifying its defense. However, Tung Wah gained an inch and pressed forward step by step. At this time, the Zhenhuan defenders were already enraged, repeatedly wanting to counterattack, but they were insufficient in strength. Finally, surrounded on all sides, trapped on the left and right, relying on several struggles, they failed to turn danger into safety. Jin Adu, eager for his team, mistakenly went it alone. A few paces in front of the two-door line, Feng Yunyou took the penalty kick, raised his foot and struck. The ball hit the south corner post.

Although it was escaped, it was also fortunate. Less than five minutes into the battle, Feng Yunyou got another chance to take a penalty kick. The ball brushed the top of the door and went out at an angle. The Zhenbao team was indeed lucky, but the accuracy of Tung Wah's vanguard's shot left the audience disappointed. Tung Wah, seeing that the attack was fruitless, also relaxed. Zhenbao, seeing that their own luck was prosperous, bet that the battle would definitely be victorious. The forwards joined forces in one place and attacked from the left. With the help of Ge Chengbao, Wu Guicheng took advantage of the situation and struck, heading straight for the Tung Wah gate. Lu Zhongen failed to stop it, and was surrounded by Zhenhuan's forwards. A burst of mud and smoke rose everywhere. Therefore,

It was also a failure for Zhenhuan to attack the gate. Wu Guicheng sent a corner kick. Wang Jingxi and Zhang Zhizhen rushed forward to attack the gate, but both were shut out. But it annoyed the Tung Wah defender Li Ning. One foot stood firmly, and one foot was energized, aiming at the ball, and it was a kick. Vanguard Fu Zhibin saw an opportunity in the front line and fell back, so the ball landed next to Fu. As soon as it was said, the little ball rolled along the ground towards Zhen's empty city, and the goalkeeper could not save it, so he was hit by a ball,

After the re-opening, Zhenhuan tried hard to counterattack, but ultimately failed to immediately recapture the city due to low morale. In the first half, Tung Wah ate twice as much, and after moisturizing their throats with lime, they changed defenses and fought each other, and their energy was restored, which was even more exciting. Before the battle had begun for a moment, Li Yichen charged into the heavy group alone and attacked the mountain gate fiercely. The ball was fast and low, rubbing the ground and shooting in. By the time Zhen's goalkeeper stood firm, he knew that

Tung Wah's army came to invade the territory again after 15 minutes. Dai Linjing led the army and rushed back and forth, taking advantage of the smoke to break in. The gate of Zhenhuan was in chaos for a while, and all the rescue was obtained, but they were not hit. Finally, they were annoyed, and Li Yichen made a comeback, and Wan Xianghua took the opportunity to attack from the side, so that

At this time, Zhenhuan was calling in vain, unable to attack and unable to realize the retreat. So they changed their tactics and made a sound in the east and attacked in the west, and it worked. Li Fenglou intercepted the ball and sent it out in one foot. Guan Yongkuan continued to rotate and go up, and went straight to Huanglong. Tung Wah team was not easy to transfer back because the large army was outside, resulting in an empty city, and it was too heavy on the enemy after the victory, and there were only two defenders, the goalkeeper and Li Ning, and it was difficult to stop the enemy. At this time, the surrounding spectators shouted and cheered, and the sound of refueling was endless, but the Zhenhuan team was exhausted and hoarse because they had been fighting against the enemy for a long time, and they were unable to do anything. Results of the 7th Guangdong Provincial Aquatic Sports Meet

Yang Hsiu-chiung Breaks National Record in Women's 100-Meter Backstroke with a Time of 1 Minute 40 Seconds

(Special Dispatch from Guangzhou) The 7th Guangdong Provincial Aquatic Sports Meet was held at the Guangzhou Aquatic Sports Association swimming pool in Dongshan on the 21st of this month. Lasting three days, the meet included seventeen men's teams, 144 male athletes, ten women's teams, and 28 female athletes, totaling 172 male and female athletes. The venue was newly decorated, with the aquatic sports field located on the riverbank. The honorary seats and press box were to the north, the music stage was upstairs, the conference office and athlete assembly area were to the west, and the team spectator stands were to the south. The opening ceremony was held at 8:00 AM on the 21st. After the ceremony, all athletes gathered in front of the podium to take an oath, which read: "(I, Yu Jing, in my amateur capacity, will恪守总理提倡体育之遗训 abide by the late Premier's advocacy of physical education and the regulations of this association, participate in competitions to achieve the goal of strengthening the race and the nation. I solemnly swear.)" After the oath, the competition began.

Thousands of spectators attended that day. After each event, uplifting music was played, and applause thundered, creating a lively atmosphere. According to statistics, the most notable event on the first day was Yang Hsiu-chiung breaking her own national record of 1 minute 45.2 seconds in the 100-meter backstroke with a time of 1 minute 40 seconds. Other records broken included the men's 100-meter backstroke, 200-meter breaststroke, and men's and women's 200-meter relay. On the second day, the men's 400-meter breaststroke also set a new provincial record. As for the artistic diving, the various forms were dazzling. The athletes in the waves each showed their skills, earning much applause from the audience. The third day was entirely dedicated to the finals of various events. The atmosphere at the swimming pool was very tense. Moreover, as the day coincided with the Mid-Autumn Festival and Sunday, the audience was even more crowded, with no empty seats. The male athletes also considered this day crucial for winning titles, so everyone fought bravely, agile as swimming dragons. The men were able to break the old provincial records in three events: the 400-meter freestyle, 400-meter breaststroke, and 400-meter relay. Around 3:00 PM, the water polo finals concluded, and awards were presented. By the time the closing ceremony took place, it was already after 6:00 PM. The results and total scores of each event over the three days are listed as follows:

Education News

Wuxi and Shanghai to Establish Labor Education Experimental Zones

Officials from the Ministries of Industry and Education to Arrive in Wuxi First on Monday

Following the decision of the Labor Education Design Committee, jointly established by the Ministries of Industry and Education, to establish five labor education experimental zones in Shanghai, Wuxi, Tianjin, Qingdao, and Hankou, the Ministries dispatched section chiefs Yang Fang from the Ministry of Industry and Zhong Lingxiu from the Ministry of Education to Wuxi and Shanghai last week to guide the establishment of these two labor education experimental zones. After these two zones are established, they will proceed to Tianjin, Qingdao, Hankou, and other places to provide guidance. It is now reported that Yang Fang, the section chief dispatched by the Ministry of Industry, and Zhong Lingxiu, the section chief from the Ministry of Education, have agreed to depart from Beijing for Wuxi on the morning of next Monday (October 1st) to inspect the state of labor education in that area (where some labor education facilities already exist). They will then, in accordance with Article 3 of the Experimental Zone Organization Regulations (which stipulates that a guidance committee of seven to nine members should be established in the labor education experimental zone to organize the committee and oversee labor education experimental affairs in the zone, with committee members selected and appointed by the Ministries of Industry and Education from the following organizations: (1) the Labor Education Design Committee; (2) the local governing body; (3) the local Party headquarters; (4) the local labor organizations; (5) the local employers' organizations; (6) the local social education organizations), negotiate the organization of the local labor education experimental zone and request various parties to nominate members for the guidance committee, for them to bring back to the two Ministries for review and appointment. After spending several days in Wuxi to complete negotiations with various parties and other related matters, they will proceed to Shanghai to inspect the state of labor education there and then discuss the organization of the Shanghai labor education experimental zone. After completing these matters in a few days, they will return to the Ministry. The labor education experimental zones in Tianjin, Qingdao, and Hankou will be attended to later, with the two Ministries dispatching officials to provide guidance and supervision. The fourteen articles of the Labor Education Experimental Zone Organization Regulations, previously announced by the Ministries of Industry and Education, are excerpted below with the important articles recorded: (Article 1) To experiment with and promote the implementation of labor education, the Ministries of Industry and Education designate appropriate industrial areas to establish labor education experimental zones, referred to as the "Ministry of Industry and Education Labor Education [Location] Experimental Zone." (Article 2) The experimental zone shall be under the direction and supervision of the Ministries of Industry and Education with regard to labor education experimental matters. (Article 3) (See the full text of Article 3 above, within parentheses). (Article 4) Members of the experimental zone guidance committee shall serve on a voluntary basis. (Article 5) The experimental zone guidance committee shall have one director, responsible for all affairs. The director shall be selected by the Ministries of Industry and Education from among the committee members. (Article 6) The tasks of the experimental zone guidance committee are as follows: (1) To formulate a labor education implementation plan for the zone, based on the outline of the labor education implementation methods; (2) To promote the meaning of labor education and its relationship; (3) To investigate out-of-school laborers in the zone and urge them to attend school; (4) To establish labor schools or labor classes and other venues for implementing labor education; (5) To raise funds for promoting labor education within the zone; (6) To prepare the zone's budget and final accounts for promoting labor education; (7) Other matters relating to the promotion of labor education in the zone. (Article 9) The experimental zone guidance committee may fully utilize the following personnel as teachers and staff for labor schools or labor classes and other venues for implementing labor education in the zone: (1) Officials of local governing bodies; (2) Officials of local Party headquarters; (3) Officials of local labor organizations; (4) Employees of local factories; (5) Local primary school teachers; (6) Interns from local normal schools; (7) Other enthusiastic individuals. (Article 10) Laborers within the experimental zone shall be required to enroll in school in stages. Those with special circumstances must obtain permission from the experimental zone guidance committee and report to the Ministries of Industry and Education for verification. (Article 11) The funds for promoting labor education in the experimental zone, in addition to the provisions of Article 13 of the outline of the labor education implementation methods, may be raised by the experimental zone guidance committee from local government agencies, labor organizations, and other social groups or private individuals. (Remaining articles omitted)

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

New Type of Loudspeaker

— One Who Knows

Ordinary driving system dynamic loudspeakers have shortcomings when used in powerful amplifiers. First, when the voice coil moves in the gap of the magnetic field, its intensity is often greater at the inner end than at the outer end, making it difficult to balance and easily causing sound distortion. Second, the flexible wire connectors between the matching transformer and the voice coil are prone to interruptions.

Radio researchers have recently discovered an improved new type of loudspeaker. The principle and usage method were published in the American "Radio Amateur" magazine. A brief translation and introduction are provided here, as shown in Figures A and B. A is a special type of armature made of silicon steel sheets from a transformer L1, L2, L3, and L4. The four coils are wound on this armature. These four coils are connected as shown in the figure. The two ends of L1 and L4 are connected to the plates of the push-pull amplifier's two vacuum tubes as the output circuit (similar to the primary coil of a transformer). LM is a movable voice coil. This new type of loudspeaker is slightly different from ordinary dynamic loudspeakers in terms of structure and effect. The structure is simpler, and its magnetic field is automatically excited by the strong plate current, which is proportional to the intensity of the sound wave current.

A B C

The voice coil LM is a closed-circuit inductance placed in the center of the iron core, as shown in Figures A, B, and C. The double-arrow shape in the figure indicates the direction of the DC flow of the plate current, which is used to excite the magnetic field. The single-arrow shape indicates the direction of the instantaneous AC current variation. The magnetic field is connected to the armature by DC current, making the intensity fixed, which is represented by solid lines. The magnetic field is input by the audio AC current from the plate current, resulting in a changing state, which is represented by dashed lines. The change in the magnetic lines of force in the middle of the armature causes the induction voice coil (also known as the dynamic coil) to form an AC circuit. The magnetic lines of force of this fixed magnetic field have an opposite effect on the induced current of the LM voice coil, causing the voice coil to move. This movement direction can be forward or backward, like a piston on a steam engine; or it can be circular, like an armature on an electric motor; however, this depends on how the four fixed coils are connected.

If one wants to make one of the above two actions, such as piston action, then the connection method is as shown in Figure C.

Causes of Open Circuits in Low-Frequency Transformers

— Li Yuanqing

Everyone knows the importance of low-frequency transformers in radios and broadcasting equipment. However, they have a very annoying problem: they are often prone to open circuits.

Initially, most people thought that the reason for transformer open circuits was that the wires used were too thin and burned out due to current overload. However, the fact is not that simple.

Someone spent twelve US dollars to buy a large low-frequency transformer (wound with thicker wires), thinking that they could rest easy. Who knew that it would fail within a week! Later, they replaced it with a small transformer worth only two Chinese dollars, but it continued to work perfectly for more than ten months.

Over the years, the author has wound many low-frequency transformers using wires of different thicknesses and conducted dozens of experiments. The results show that:

Only a small number of low-frequency transformer failures are caused by current overload. The majority of failures are caused by corrosion due to moisture.

This is not just hearsay; there is evidence to prove it:

1. The primary coil of a typical low-frequency transformer is usually wound with 40-gauge wire. Although the specified allowable current for this type of wire is only 0.06 amperes, it actually requires a current of more than three amperes to burn it out.

2. Two transformers wound with the same gauge wire, one used in the detector tube (i.e., the first stage of low-frequency amplification, usually with a plate current of about one milliampere), and the other used as an output transformer for the final stage power tube (usually with a plate current of more than 30 milliamperes). In theory, the second one should fail first, but in fact, the opposite is often true! Isn't this strange?

In fact, the reason is very simple. As mentioned above, most transformer failures are caused by corrosion due to moisture. We know that heat is proportional to the square of the current (Heat = l2Rt). In other words, the greater the current passing through the wire, the higher the temperature generated. High temperatures keep the transformer dry, making it less susceptible to moisture and less likely to corrode.

If the reader doesn't believe it, they can disassemble a damaged transformer and carefully examine the location of the open circuit. They will often easily find green mold spots, but rarely see any signs of burning. Isn't this obvious proof?

As for the reasons why the wires corrode, I must also add a word:

1. Careless winding Many crudely made transformers have their coils wound by hand. If the worker winding the coils has acidic substances or sweat on their hands, then the occurrence of corrosion is to be expected.

2. Improper soldering When soldering the ends of the transformer coils, one should absolutely avoid using fluxes containing acids. Otherwise, corrosion will inevitably occur over time, leading to an open circuit.

3. Insecure sealing No matter how carefully you wind and solder the transformer, if the sealing is not secure, it will be damaged by external moisture over time. Transformers are particularly prone to damage during the rainy season for this reason. Some well-sealed transformers, it is said, can be immersed in water for more than a month without being affected at all.

4. Improper location If the radio is placed in a damp place or near a wall, then the chance of an open circuit will naturally be particularly high.

In addition, severe vibrations, internal short circuits, or sudden interruptions of plate current during use can all cause an open circuit. Due to space limitations, I will not elaborate further here.

Several Uses of a Useful Thing - Shellac

— Mediocre Words

Shellac is a type of foreign dry lacquer, commonly sold in paint stores at a very low price. This substance has many uses in radio, as it can be used as a highly insulating paint and as a "universal adhesive." I will briefly describe a few of its uses below:

Before using shellac, it should first be dissolved in alcohol. Take any amount of alcohol, place it in a glass bottle, and then place the glass bottle in hot water to warm it. Then add a small amount of shellac, dissolving and adding until it no longer dissolves, to obtain a shellac alcohol solution, which can be used for the following purposes.

A. Method of making bakelite substitutes Take dry plywood and apply the shellac alcohol solution two or three times to obtain a bakelite substitute that is easy to drill holes in and not easy to crack.

B. Self-made insulation wire method Take several feet of 18-gauge double silk-covered wire, apply the shellac alcohol solution two or three times, and wait for it to dry to obtain inexpensive, high-quality, and convenient insulation wire, which is ideal for soldering radios.

C. Use as a fixing agent for wires The shape of the coils in wavemeters and shortwave radios must not be changed in the slightest, so as not to change their inductance. You can apply the shellac alcohol solution two or three times so that their shape will not change.

D. Repairing cracks in the paper cone of a loudspeaker You can also apply this substance to repair cracks in the paper cone of a loudspeaker, so that the sound can be as clear as usual.

E. Universal adhesive Shellac is a universal adhesive that can be used to bond almost any solid material (including metal), and the joints are not afraid of moisture. For example, if a bakelite board is cracked, you can apply the shellac alcohol solution to the cracks, put the broken pieces together and let it sit, and it will bond tightly when dry.

Marconi's New Invention - Radio Lighthouse

— Lv Zhong

Radio inventor Marconi stood in the pilot house of his yacht, the "Electra," which he used for experiments, with a triumphant smile on a certain day last month, testing his recently successfully invented radio lighthouse (Theradioligboncuse) to guide the yacht. The windows of the yacht's pilot house were completely covered with curtains, so that the outside could not be seen. Marconi and the captain blindly drove, and were able to safely enter the Italian port of Sesinilevante.

Marconi's development of radio has saved the lives of millions of people in distress. However, this radio lighthouse can save millions of steamers when they enter port in dense fog and heavy rain, to avoid the disaster of collisions. Therefore, Marconi called it a great invention.

The experiment set up an ultra-shortwave transmitting station on a cape 300 feet high on the sea surface at the entrance of the port of Sesinilevante; there were also two radio lighthouses (please refer to the attached figure) with small shortwave transmitters placed on two floating stations at the entrance of the harbor, about 300 feet apart.

There was a receiver on the yacht, equipped with two indicators; one was visible, with an instrument like an electric meter, and the pointer on the meter moved to the left or right depending on the direction the ship was sailing; the other was audible, indicating from the loudspeaker that the ship's direction was wrong.

The signal emitted by the main transmitter was relayed by the radio lighthouse and then received by the yacht. When the ship continued to sail in the direction of the target location between the two radio lighthouses, the pointer on the indicator would point directly to the center. If the pointer was deflected to one side, it meant that the ship's direction was too far to the left or too far to the right. When the "Electra" yacht safely entered the port, Marconi and the captain were driving blindly, never observing the coastline or pilot lines. Marconi said: "Every port in the world will definitely use this radio direction finder in the next few years."

The audible indicator can emit two kinds of signals from the loudspeaker, one is high-pitched and the other is low-pitched. When the ship is sailing in the direction of the target location, the signal always remains at a normal pitch. But if the ship deviates to one side, the loudspeaker will emit a high-pitched or low-pitched sound, warning the driver to pay attention to how the course is wrong on the visible indicator.

Modification of a Radio Phonograph Connector

— Lin Guiling

After seeing Mr. Mingxiang's excellent work (Radio Phonograph Connector) in the 71st issue of this magazine, the author thought about making one, but was troubled by the lack of spare parts. So I modified it and took the spare parts completely from an old radio. According to the test results, the performance is indeed good. When connected to a homemade TRF AC five-tube radio, the sound is very loud, similar to receiving a local 100-watt or more radio station with an antenna, which is much better than connecting to the grid circuit of the detector tube.

Fellow sufferers! Comrades who are troubled by the constraints of spare parts, you may wish to try it when you have time.

This is just a reference. I hope comrades will use your intelligence to make more improvements. Maybe you will find even better results?

Note: Please refer to Mr. Mingxiang's excellent work in the 71st issue of this magazine for the method of use.

Parts list:

CI 2 MFD fixed capacitor

R 750 ohm fixed resistor

V No. 33 powerful output tube

L Use 2.5-inch tube with 28-gauge enameled wire to wind 100 turns for LI, and tap one end at 50 turns for connecting to B battery. Separate LI by 1 point and wind 25 turns with the same gauge wire as L

Gold Standard Falls Again

| To 908 Yuan |

The Hope for a New Record Has Yet to Disappear

Buyers Helpless, Resulting in Another Drop of 7.6 Yuan

The gold market's downward trend continues. Yesterday, it created a new low price of 908 yuan, which has frightened people and depressed the market atmosphere. In one day, the downward trend was miserable, and the hope for a new record has yet to disappear. In the early morning, although the London and New York silver markets rose slightly, the increase was not much. London spot gold rose by 1.5 pence, and the exchange rate opened weaker but closed stronger. American cotton continued to fall, while American wheat rose, and stocks also rose. Preliminary trading opened steadily, rising slightly to 22-23 yuan. However, the fact that the English and Japanese banks reportedly closed lower at .0625 after the market closed, even though there was a slight increase today, still made people generally feel unfavorable and start selling. It once fell into the 20 yuan range, but demand exceeded supply at low prices, so it gradually pulled up after the market opened. At this time, people's hearts were stable, so although the banks were tight, the domestic market was still tight. The news that HSBC's exchange rates for the US and the UK remained unchanged caused buyers to become active and rise, but the overall trend did not show a reversal. The phenomenon stopped at high prices, and the bulls still wavered, so a fluctuating situation appeared. People's hearts were like walking on thin ice. As soon as there were sellers, the downward trend intensified. When the 20 yuan range was broken, the selling intensified even more. Even if there were people maintaining at low prices, they were no match for the crowd. Sellers followed one after another, and people's hopes for a new record became more obvious. The exchange rate also became stronger, and the downward trend became more difficult to control. Although there was no special news, rumors slightly deteriorated, and it gradually fell. Later, Chinese merchants continued to fill US dollars, and the forward price even hardened to 37 yuan, making it difficult to sell, and even broke the 10 yuan range, creating a new low price of 908 yuan. Short covering slightly started, and the banks took the opportunity to force up, allowing the gold market to rise by 5 yuan. Unexpectedly, a telegram from Bombay reported a rise of 9 annas, and selling started again, but the 10 yuan range was difficult to break again. Soon, the rumor that the Central Bank was opening spot positions spread, and the domestic market gradually tightened. Buyers showed signs of recovery, and because the second telegram from Bombay reported a retraction of 1 anna, there were signs of a turnaround. The final situation was tight and stable, and there were no special changes. Now, the market conditions for the day are recorded below.

The morning opened at 920.5 yuan, down 1.5 yuan from the previous close. The exchange rate opened with a recent selling price. Later, the situation suddenly weakened. Large customers such as Yuanyi, Yuanmaoyong, and Dalianbang sold fiercely, and the selling suddenly went crazy. Although there were scattered shorts covering at low prices, Fuxingyong also entered, once rising from 18.8 yuan to 9.9 yuan, but Fuan, Yuankangxiang, and Fuxingyong suddenly sold and fell to 6.5 yuan. Mitsui even filled US dollars at 0.75 in January. Hengyu, Fuxingyong, etc. came in and rose back to 8.5 yuan, but the market situation was extremely vague and people's hearts were miserable. The Secret of Writing Books

— Xiang Yu

In (The Art of Bookmaking) it is said that at first, he did not understand why writers without talent produced so prolifically. One day, he went to the British Museum in England and saw two types of people making books: one who specialized in collecting fragments of ancient English texts left behind by bookworms to create a book, and another who took a few lines from one book and a few lines from another to create a book. Only then did he understand the art of bookmaking.

In China (perhaps in all countries), those who write books similar to the first type are those who study tortoise shells, bronzes, and thread-bound books from the Spring and Autumn Period and the Warring States Period all the way to the Qing Dynasty. This group of scholars relies on the works of the deceased, extracting materials from them for research, explanation, and discussion to make a living. Naturally, the works of the ancients are not copyrighted. Even if you distribute them on their behalf and pocket the money, the ancients will not sue you or ask for royalties. It will definitely not be like what Owen imagined, with the ghosts of ancient writers jumping down from the walls one by one, stripping a modern professor of his clothes to reveal his true form, and exposing the secrets of a literary figure, leaving him in a sorry state! Master Yutang is, after all, an old fox (stealing royalties from the ancients to support my wife and children, what's wrong with that?) (That's the gist of it), truly revealing the mystery.

Those who write books similar to the second type are naturally people like us who make a living from newspapers and magazines. In China today, apart from purely literary publications, most of the materials in political and economic publications rely on newspapers. Therefore, the tools we need to make a living are just a few newspapers, a pair of scissors, a bottle of paste, and a scrapbook for pasting newspaper clippings. At most, we add some organizing work and use a little brainpower to explain the raw materials, and then we have a long article that can be sold for money. If this work is done consistently, after a few years, it may become a voluminous work of hundreds of thousands of words. Even though your materials are cut from newspapers with scissors, no one dares to question you or sue you.

In addition, there is another type of book writer that Owen did not mention. Perhaps in Owen's time, this was not very prevalent. But in China, this method of writing books has special advantages. That is, if you understand foreign languages, you can take the works of foreign writers and translate them entirely or copy parts of them to create your own book. China is not a member of the international copyright convention, so it is of course no problem to copy and translate the works of dead foreign writers. Even if the writer is still alive, he will not frown upon you or sue you if you copy and translate his works.

However, those who aspire to write books should never steal materials from domestic writers who are still alive. Because the works of writers who are still alive, although not very brilliant, and even stolen from others, if you steal their works and they find out, they will put on a stern face and use their authority as scholars to make things difficult for you. As a result, you will not only waste your efforts and fail to become famous, but you will also not receive any royalties, and you will eventually be unable to move forward and no longer be able to join the ranks of scholars.

That's the secret of writing books. It's not a secret, nor is it a dark secret. It's just the way things have always been.

As for the quality of a book, it does not depend on whether you plagiarize or not, but on whether you can refine and process the plagiarized materials. If you can, like Macbeth, find a piece here (frog's toe), and a piece there (lizard's tail), mix them with monkey's blood, put them in a magician's cauldron (a person's brain), and make organic food or medicine, then you will definitely be welcomed.

Wife's Hospitalization

— Hui Ying

On this day, my wife had just finished class and, according to her, still had to correct a few exercise books, but the little animal in her belly was starting to move. She was in pain for quite a while, even crying.

According to the doctor's examination, the due date was in the next few days. I became anxious and told my wife to go to the hospital to get checked and be admitted if necessary.

My wife, in great pain, got into a rickshaw (why don't we have a car?). She left, leaving me with endless fear. Two past events quickly flashed through my mind:

Didn't XX's lover die from childbirth? And wasn't Lu Yin, who recently passed away, also die from childbirth? Oh, this matter...

I dared not think about it anymore. Even so, I still seemed to see my wife groaning in pain in the hospital.

(Why didn't I go with her!) I regretted it, but after a while, I realized that this regret was unnecessary. The reason my wife went to the hospital alone, without asking me to go with her, was because she was worried about money.

Originally, people like us who have difficulty maintaining our lives have no reason to have children. God, why can't we have a child? Is having children the exclusive right of a certain type of people in this world? I don't accept it. This matter...

I was about to continue thinking, thinking of myself as a useless man who couldn't make money (actually, it's because this society doesn't give me the opportunity to make money), when my wife came back. She still had the painful belly.

(What, didn't you see the doctor?)

Seeing her like this, I quickly asked.

(The time was up.)

(Didn't I tell you to ask to be hospitalized if the time was up?)

(It costs two dollars for a special registration.)

(What, does hospitalization also require registration, a special registration?)

I really doubted this so-called semi-charitable hospital, and at the same time felt inexplicable anger. If we had money, what would two dollars be? To be honest, if we had money, we wouldn't be prepared to stay in this charitable hospital. Now, the word "charity" really needs to be re-evaluated.

My wife's belly was hurting even more severely. She couldn't speak, just bent over, holding her belly and crying. I supported her and asked:

(Then, how about going to XX Hospital? Doesn't it not require a special registration for hospitalization there?)

My wife couldn't answer, but she nodded. This time, I had to go with her. I would spend the extra rickshaw fare for one person because I didn't trust her! I really wanted to starve myself for a few days and save some money to hire a car for her to sit in, but my wife rejected my idea.

When we arrived at XX Hospital, I was very nervous, afraid of having to pay a special registration fee again. People without money are constantly thinking about money, and have simply become pitiful slaves to money. Thank God, this hospital didn't charge a special registration fee, and I felt much relieved.

Immediately afterwards, a new fear came:

(Will she pass this difficult time safely, or will she become an unfortunate victim?)

We walked into Room XXX. My wife was crying, shouting in pain. My heart was pounding. Fear, fear, what was I afraid of? ...

"Jintan, Do You Want to Buy Jintan?"

— TK

Between Friends

— Chen Bibing

Having drifted at sea for ten years, what I have heard or seen – especially what I have experienced – always makes me feel that dealing with people seems easy at first, but is actually very mysterious.

Human beings are originally divided into many kinds. There are the good, and the even better; there are the evil, and the even more evil. But most human beings are neither good nor evil.

Perhaps it is because of similar interests, or perhaps it is because of emotional closeness, that some people, originally from different environments, can actually become close friends.

And some people, who originally worked together in the same environment, nevertheless have different opinions and become enemies.

Instead of saying it is a meeting of minds, it would be better to say it is a convergence of interests. Close friends today, enemies tomorrow; enemies tomorrow, close friends the day after tomorrow. These kinds of things are really common. Originally, this is not surprising. In this age of money worship, all human relationships are material, not spiritual. Therefore, some people hold a fixed view, which is: (Everyone is bad, only money is good.) They have no sympathy for anyone. If you complain to them, they will reply, (They used to be even more painful than you.) They always think that pain is something everyone should have – even if they can help you, they are still thinking of other aspects. Their treatment of you is so harsh that it is simply indescribable. The motive for this kind of help is definitely not that they are helping you; it is that they are using your painful situation as a weakness, so they can buy a large amount of your labor with a small amount of money.

However, on the other hand, making friends does have a time and space element. Many people can only share hardship, not happiness; many people can only share happiness, but not hardship. Snobbery is inevitable in this society, even among family members, fathers, sons, and brothers, let alone friends? Therefore, some people have one face when they come to ask you for help, and another face when you go to beg them. From my own experience, when you have the means, friends will volunteer to undertake things that do not require them to bear any burden; but when you are frustrated and in trouble, friends will refuse even things that do not require much effort. If you say that this kind of behavior is snobbish, it certainly is; but if you say that his behavior is unethical, he himself will never admit it.

Furthermore, misunderstandings between friends are also inevitable. This is even more likely to happen among people who are quick-witted, rough in temperament, or experience a lot of stimulation. Very often, a major conflict arises from a very small matter – even to the point of mistaking good intentions for malice, and the deeper the love, the more intense the hate. As a result, nothing else but severing the relationship is left. This is very heartbreaking.

Even more, some people suffer from megalomania and like to lie – even to the point of fabricating things out of thin air. Sometimes financial dealings between close friends are unavoidable, but some friends use this to brag everywhere, boasting to other friends, thinking that it is the greatest generosity on his part. As a result, good intentions are only taken as malice. Money or a meal of friendship has a price, but the reputation of others has no price to estimate. Therefore, inviting friends to dinner or financial dealings are not necessarily essential means of making friends.

A gentleman's friendship is as light as water. Some people, before any accidents happen, are very plain when dealing with you, and their attitude is very moderate. When there is something to say, they will say it; when there is nothing to say, they will not deliberately flatter people. However, when any friend encounters an unexpected disaster and asks for their help, they are extremely sincere in their attitude, and they will always help you to the best of their ability. They will not despise you because you are bankrupt. On the contrary, they will have even greater sympathy for you. Their friendship will be even more in accord, exceeding the usual social interactions by more than double. These people are indeed worth befriending, but it is difficult to find one in a hundred people – most ordinary people are snobbish.

There are also some friends who are very mediocre and dispirited when they are down on their luck, but when they are successful and developed, they have an air of arrogance. Their voices become louder, their spirits become invigorated, and they even stand tall with their chests puffed out when they walk. When you go to see them, they will clearly have nothing to do, but they will pretend to be very busy, making you wait in the reception room for one or two hours, or even deliberately scolding servants in front of you to show their dignity and power.

And there are others who don't offend anyone and always have a smile on their face, but if you are in a difficult situation and ask them for a loan, they will resolutely refuse. Even if it is something they can do with no effort and that would not harm their budget in the slightest, they will refuse regardless of the reason – it is clear that you are equals, but the moment you ask them for money, they think you are vulgar and inferior to them.

But then there are some who have no money in their pockets, but when a friend asks for a loan, their pain is actually greater than that of the person borrowing the money. Some will promise to meet in the afternoon or the next day, and then pawn their clothes to help their friend.

Still others, within the scope of cheap help, may give you some non-monetary assistance, but if you ask for a loan, a single cent is impossible.

Although there are many kinds of people described above, most people in the world are neither good nor bad. They may give you a little help that requires no effort, but extravagant hopes are impossible.

Like me, I am born vulgar. I help others when I have money, and I am helped by others when I have no money. For good people, even if I know that there is no practical reward other than gratitude in my heart, I will treat them well. For bad people, even if I know that they are evil, I will have no acts of revenge other than cursing them in my heart. However, in modern society, good people always suffer losses, and bad people always gain advantages. This is why, invisibly, people are encouraged to do evil, so it is even more difficult for young people to live in the world.

Mr. Village Head (10) (4)

— Wang Renshu

Winterborn, limping, sat in the pavilion for a full hour. Mr. Village Head Feng Wen’s cries were sent from the street. Dragging himself out of a rather leisurely, and also quite noble, state, knowing that there was some errand he had to do, at that time, Winterborn, limping, waved his ginger-joint-like hand, scolding to himself and for his own hearing:

(Damn it, being a village policeman is really not a job for humans! A mangy dog!)

Winterborn, limping, resumed his cane-like walking style, and went.

Mr. Village Head Feng Wen, was at Mr. Dasheng’s Yusheng Shop.

This Yusheng Shop, was originally Mr. Feng Wen’s father’s inheritance. Now, together with the house, utensils and goods, it was all sold to Mr. Dasheng.

Mr. Feng Wen didn’t have capital, couldn’t match the goods; and also couldn’t afford to match the goods. Three copper coins for yellow sugar, two copper coins for needles, most buyers were so piecemeal. But if you ran into a brick wall with the buyers a few times, the buyers would come to your door less. Mr. Feng Wen’s era of Yusheng Shop, just went out like that.

Mr. Dasheng, however, had a plan.

For years, the village had been plagued by floods every year. (The mid-July great flood had already become an old saying. But when a flood occurred, the bridges and dikes everywhere were always washed away in large part. The great flood of mid-July the year before broke the rule; a Chang'an Bridge at the head of Niutou Village, which had not been washed down for decades, was actually washed away (broke the water).

Chang'an Bridge was a huge building more than ten zhang high. Entirely made of square blocks of stone slabs. A continuous series of five large ring holes. At the junction of ring hole and ring hole, were built rows of (water breakers). Triangle cones that looked like that, with the pointed mouths facing outwards, breaking and dividing the water flow.

That day, three days after the great flood, Mr. Dasheng led the clan chief, standing on the bridge looking. Stone railings surrounded both sides of the bridge, and each stone pillar was carved with a lion, white elephant, and the like. Mr. Dasheng hugged the stone pillar, sighing and saying:

(If we don't repair this water breaker this year, perhaps next year this arch bridge will be difficult to preserve.)

(Yes.) The clan chief, as usual, took Mr. Dasheng's opinion as his own.

(If this arch bridge is not preserved, my grandfather's efforts will have been wasted, not to mention; the feng shui of Niutou Village will also be broken.

(It should be repaired, it should be repaired, feng shui is important.) The clan chief answered even more affirmatively.

Supplement of Shenbao 本埠

Talks

Arms Dealers Manipulate Congressional Elections

— Min

Not many days ago, according to reports, the US Senate Arms Investigation Committee discovered that US arms dealers have a secret to manipulate congressional elections. This can be said to be a major disgrace in recent democratic politics. In fact, the secrets of so-called democratic politics have long been spied by the general public. The so-called congressmen are nothing more than tools of a few capitalists. This point has long been clearly known to the world. And now, the fact that US arms dealers manipulate congressional elections proves even more clearly what so-called democratic politics really is.

However, there is an even more important point here. What kind of politics does the manipulation of congressional elections by arms dealers represent? Obviously, this means that the current politics, not only in the United States, but in any country in the world, have embarked on the most tense stage of war preparations. Therefore, arms dealers are responding to this political trend and are particularly active. The activity of arms dealers precisely indicates that the present is an era in urgent need of arms; arms in this era are the most needed necessities of any country in the world. In this way, we can see how the world today is being pushed day by day into a very thick cloud of war.

Raincoat

— Hong Ben

I suddenly woke up from the shock of rain hitting the window lattice and realized that today was the third day of registration, and things were so busy that I had to hurry. I planned to find a way to compensate for this loss in the future.

I wiped my face hastily and saw that the watch was already half past seven. If I didn't hurry, I wouldn't be able to squeeze through the crowded office door. So I took two steps at a time and walked down the three turns and eighteen bends of the building, standing still at the door. The rain was pouring down. I just thought that if this rain had fallen a month and a half earlier, it would not only be a welcome rain, but literally a drop of rice, a life. I waited and waited, but the rain fell even harder. Looking at my watch again, it was already a quarter past eight. I had no choice but to brave the rain and run to the office. The office was so far from the dormitory that I ran for about five minutes, panting heavily before I got there, my whole body already like a drowned chicken. Fortunately, the rain lessened during lunch, so I returned to the dormitory. After changing my clothes, I thought of two things to avoid the rain, one was an umbrella (sun umbrella or rain umbrella), and the other was a raincoat. I originally had both of these things, but the umbrella was borrowed by a friend, so I thought of the raincoat that had been in my suitcase for a long time.

Speaking of this raincoat, it had always been (prepared but not used), but this time it was necessary to take it out. Coincidentally, the rain started pouring down again after lunch. At this time, I was fearless. When office hours arrived, I put on my raincoat and ran downstairs. But because I lacked a rain hat on my head, I still had to run fast when I walked out the door. When I got to the office and took off my raincoat, I found that my clothes were as wet as when I ran in the rain.

So I hesitated. Because it was the last day of registration and it was raining heavily, there were very few people registering in the afternoon. I took advantage of this free time to concentrate on thinking about why the raincoat couldn't keep out the rain. Although the goods were not fashionable, the material was good, and it was brand new, even though it had been in the suitcase for almost two years and had never been formally used. I thought about it for a long time, but the answer was still not very reliable. A raincoat is definitely for keeping out the rain, and it can keep out the rain. But the facts were too disturbing. My brand new raincoat couldn't keep out the rain.

After leaving the office and returning to the dormitory, I thought about it for a long time before I understood the reason.

Probably (actually, I should use a definitive term) people in the city wear raincoats in the rain also view it as a decoration, or at least as something fun to wear. If a fashionable person strolls slowly in the rain, letting their expensive clothes get wet in front of everyone, they will inevitably be scolded as (stupid). If they scurry around in the streets, they may avoid getting their clothes wet, but they will inevitably be ridiculed as (idiots), (country bumpkins). Neither of these is a good solution.

But most people in the city have such a strange temper that they don't like to use umbrellas in the rain. Just look at the Western-dressed friends who are busy in the streets. Who is carrying an umbrella? Although umbrellas are good for keeping out the rain, people in the city view them as warts. In order to avoid the above two kinds of embarrassment, they put on raincoats and abandon the tacky umbrella, not caring if their clothes get wet.

In fact, the name of this raincoat is not wrong, but it can't keep out the rain. It is originally a special product for rich gentlemen. For example, when they are traveling in the rain in a car or charter, from indoors to the car, or from the car to the room, they are afraid that one or two drops of water will drip onto their clothes or neck, making them uncomfortable, so they wear raincoats to shield themselves. People like this naturally need to use this kind of raincoat. Otherwise, raincoats are useless. But people in the city like to imitate (the style of the Duke of Mandeville), so everyone wears them, and it becomes a kind of decoration for rainy days.

Change

— Jin Ren

I accidentally found a faded photo in a suitcase that had traveled through three passes and six docks. It was a photo I took when I graduated from elementary school. The back was marked with the words "Taken in the summer of the ninth year of the Republic of China in XX, etc." I was happy for a while and put it in the mirror frame on my desk. Compared with my most recent photo, there was simply no resemblance.

From the ninth year of the Republic of China to now, this long distance, I have changed in every way. People say to me; of course, I myself am very clear about understanding that I have gone from the innocent childhood to the middle age formed by society. This gradual change, the dissimilarity of the two photos is only on the surface. But to what extent have I changed? The most obvious is that I was driven out of my family. This kind of family conflict, I don't need to use the facts as a basis, I was so wrong that I couldn't stand in my hometown. So I started to change.

This suitcase of mine can be used as strong evidence. Its clean surroundings have been swallowed up by the names of many stations and wharves; as for whether the owner of this suitcase has become equally unclear, some people are eager to come forward to prove it, saying: (You don't even want your family, I really can't see that this child would change like this!) Naturally, I have changed like this, and the two photos have nothing in common!

This time, by a chance opportunity, many of my childhood companions gathered together. Apart from the fact that I had changed to this state, I felt that everyone had changed. If a photo taken at that time had not been lost, I think everyone who saw it would have shouted: (I have changed!) But our three days together were still like when we were kids, talking and laughing, messing around, taking small advantages, and it was as if no one had changed; and one of our oldest sisters said: (Jin Di still has the same old temper.)

It can be seen that I have not changed to (this state). So I carefully played with the two photos, wanting to solve this question of change or no change. The person who said I had changed to (this state), naturally he saw that I was already (this state), otherwise, I have no conflict of interest with him at all, why would he say that? The sister who said I still have the same old temper, we grew up together. After being separated for so many years, her words are naturally not to make fun of me after we met for three days; so, how to solve this problem?

Change or no change depends on me personally. I can't change or not change because people say I change or not change. Although these two photos have nothing in common, wasn't it me (one) who took the photos? Then what does change or no change have to do with other people? (Excerpt from diary)

Wandering the Streets of Shanghai on an Autumn Night

— A Wanderer

Autumn night, wandering the streets of Shanghai.

Due to business, I missed a train; looking for a friend, I ran into a wall. Thus, under the chilling autumn wind, I ended up tasting the flavor of this great city’s black magic night.

Because of the cold shrinking of my wallet, enjoying

Page 23

pleasures in this great city is not meant for me. Where should I go? For someone used to living in the countryside, and also facing economic panic, it’s truly difficult to decide!

So I bought a book and sat in a tea house for a full two hours. Lonely, I immersed my soul in the book. Suddenly startled, I realized the clock on the wall was pointing to eleven. (Find a place to sleep.) With a decision made, I strolled onto the streets of Shanghai.

I saw that streetcars were gradually becoming sparse, but the cars of the wealthy seemed not to have decreased. A gust of autumn night's cold wind blew around me, and I suddenly felt very cold. Women of the night crowded the streetsides, smiling and soliciting customers. A wave of urban shudder rose in my heart.

(What are the nights like at the dance halls?)

Suddenly, a strange feeling rose in my heart. So I strolled to the edge of the Racecourse, the grand opening of the Paramount Theatre had just finished dispersing its customers, and cars lined up and drove off. The small entrance of the Grand Shanghai Ballroom caught my eye, and the solemn class structure intimidated me. I turned around. I ran to the Metropole. Upon entering, I saw clusters of ghosts rolling around under dim lights. Then I suddenly turned around again; I was once again spat out onto the streets of Shanghai.

(What to do?)

(Better find a place to sleep.)

So I wandered aimlessly on Nanjing Road. I saw that cars were becoming increasingly sparse; people were also much fewer. I dragged my footsteps step by step, feeling the heaviness of my legs. Upon reaching the Huangpu Bund, a burst of greyish-white moonlight suddenly brought a cold autumn wind, I shivered, and woke up my dazed mind.

(How did I end up here?)

(Call a rickshaw, my legs are a bit out of control!)

So I sat in the car, passing through the heart of Shanghai at night. The cold, desolate streets really made me suspect that this was not urban Shanghai. And the constant cold wind made me shiver even more.

The Suzhou Creek lay in Shanghai’s heart in dim slumber. A beggar pulled my rickshaw, receiving two copper coins from my longing for sleep.

(You, a lowly citizen of the city, why weren't you born as the son of a wealthy family?)

Just as I was ridiculing my own stupid words in my stomach, the car stopped in front of the Jiande Apartment.

I rang the bell, and settled myself in a room.

Shanghai, is Shanghai for the rich! Not to mention the petty bourgeoisie, even a small asset class person has no blessings to enjoy the nights of Shanghai.

The taste of a night of wandering, is deeply imprinted in my heart.
